## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the rate of change of concentration (dA/dt) as a function of time and concentration in a chemical reaction. This is a classic chemical kinetics problem where the rate law relates the reaction rate to the concentration of reactants, possibly with time-dependent effects.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- {'name': 'Zero-order rate law', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0', 'scenario': 'Reaction rate independent of concentration'}
- {'name': 'First-order rate law', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A', 'scenario': 'Rate proportional to concentration (radioactive decay, first-order reactions)'}
- {'name': 'Second-order rate law', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**2', 'scenario': 'Bimolecular reaction with single species'}
- {'name': 'nth-order rate law', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**c1', 'scenario': 'General power-law kinetics with fractional or integer order'}
- {'name': 'Mixed-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2', 'scenario': 'Competing first and second order reaction pathways'}
- {'name': 'Reversible first-order reaction', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1', 'scenario': 'First-order forward reaction with reverse reaction approaching equilibrium'}
- {'name': 'Autocatalytic reaction', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A)', 'scenario': 'Logistic-type autocatalysis where product catalyzes the reaction'}
- {'name': 'Saturation kinetics (substrate inhibition)', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2)', 'scenario': 'Enzyme kinetics with substrate inhibition'}
- {'name': 'Time-dependent first-order decay', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t)', 'scenario': 'Rate constant changing with time (e.g., catalyst deactivation)'}
- {'name': 'Consecutive reaction intermediate', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * exp(c3 * t)', 'scenario': 'Rate of intermediate species in consecutive A→B→C reactions'}
- {'name': 'Polynomial rate with offset', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 + c3 * A**3', 'scenario': 'General polynomial expansion of rate law for complex mechanisms'}
- {'name': 'Square root kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**0.5', 'scenario': 'Half-order kinetics from surface reactions or dissociative mechanisms'}
- {'name': 'Rational rate law', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (1 + c2 * A)', 'scenario': 'Langmuir-Hinshelwood type surface reaction kinetics'}

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative rate of change (consumption) → dA_dt typically has negative coefficient times positive powers of A
- Equilibrium approach → Rate expression includes both negative and positive terms (forward and reverse contributions), e.g., c0*A + c1
- Integer reaction order → Power of A matches molecularity of elementary step (1 for unimolecular, 2 for bimolecular)
- Fractional reaction order → Suggests complex mechanism or surface-mediated reaction, use A**c with non-integer c
- Rate independent of time explicitly → Suggests simple rate law dA_dt = f(A) only; time dependence enters implicitly through A(t)
- Explicit time dependence in rate → Suggests external forcing, catalyst deactivation, or photochemical effects
- Autocatalytic/sigmoidal kinetics → Product of A and (constant - A) giving logistic-type behavior
- Competing parallel reactions → Sum of power-law terms with different orders: c0*A**n1 + c1*A**n2
